***oprit.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:oprit.html>oprit</a> (9375)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:oprit.html>oprit</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:oprit.html>opritten</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:oprit.html>opritje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>driveway</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p>The <a href = vnd.unilang:words.html>words</a> "<a href = vnd.unilang:oprit.html>oprit</a>" and "<a href = vnd.unilang:oprijlaan.html>oprijlaan</a>" have almost the same meaning, but the latter <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> used only for relatively long, wide and / or grand driveways, such as those leading to a palace or mansion.
</p>
